# big-code-k8s-bug-001: Missing ResourceSlice Event Handler in Kubernetes Scheduler

## Task

Investigate a bug in the Kubernetes scheduler where pods requesting Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) devices become permanently stuck in an Unschedulable state when the DRA driver starts after the pod is created. Trace the execution path through the scheduler's event-driven re-queuing architecture to identify why ResourceSlice creation/update events are silently dropped.

## Context

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.30.0 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/kubernetes--v1.30.0 (mirror of kubernetes/kubernetes) (Go, ~3.5M LOC)
- **Category**: Bug Investigation
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Entry Point**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` — `ScheduleOne()` method

## Symptom

When a pod requests a DRA device and the DRA driver starts *after* the pod is created, the pod becomes permanently stuck in `Pending` with reason `Unschedulable`. The scheduler logs `"cannot allocate all claims"` because no ResourceSlices exist at scheduling time. After the driver starts and publishes ResourceSlice objects, the pod should be rescheduled — but it never is.

The bug is a race condition: if the driver starts first, scheduling succeeds immediately. But if the pod arrives before the driver, the scheduler never retries because ResourceSlice events are not wired into the scheduling queue's re-evaluation mechanism.

## Requirements

1. Starting from the entry point, trace the execution path to the root cause
2. Identify the specific file(s) and line(s) where the bug originates
3. Explain WHY the bug occurs — focus on the event handler registration mechanism and the scheduling queue's re-evaluation trigger
4. Propose a fix with specific code changes

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- path/to/file1.ext — examined for [reason]
- path/to/file2.ext — examined for [reason]
...

## Dependency Chain
1. Symptom observed in: path/to/symptom.ext
2. Called from: path/to/caller.ext (function name)
3. Bug triggered by: path/to/buggy.ext (function name, line ~N)
...

## Root Cause
- **File**: path/to/root_cause.ext
- **Function**: function_name()
- **Line**: ~N
- **Explanation**: [Why this code is buggy]

## Proposed Fix
```diff
- buggy code
+ fixed code
```

## Analysis
[Detailed trace from symptom to root cause, explaining each step]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- Root cause identification: Did you find the correct file(s) where the bug originates?
- Call chain accuracy: Did you trace the correct path from symptom to root cause?
- Fix quality: Is the proposed fix correct and minimal?

44-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed the investigation and analysis. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

I've traced the Kubernetes scheduler bug through the event-driven re-queuing architecture and identified the root cause. The analysis has been saved to `/logs/agent/solution.md`.

### The Bug
Pods requesting Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) devices become permanently stuck in an `Unschedulable` state when the DRA driver starts after the pod is created. The scheduler should re-evaluate the pod when ResourceSlice objects (which advertise available resources) are created, but it never does.

### Root Cause
**ResourceSlice events are silently dropped** due to missing event handler wiring across three layers:

1. **`pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`** — ResourceSlice is not defined as a GVK constant and is missing from the `UnrollWildCardResource()` function

2. **`pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`** — The `addAllEventHandlers()` function has no case for `framework.ResourceSlice`, so no informer handler is registered

3. **`pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`** — The `EventsToRegister()` method doesn't include ResourceSlice events, so the plugin never signals the queue to retry pods

### The Fix
Add ResourceSlice support at all three layers following existing patterns for other DRA resources (ResourceClaim, ResourceClass, etc.):
- Define `ResourceSlice GVK` constant
- Add ResourceSlice to `UnrollWildCardResource()` 
- Register event handler in eventhandlers.go
- Add ResourceSlice event registration in the DRA plugin

The solution document contains detailed diffs for each fix location.

\\n859: // selectHost takes a prioritized list of nodes and then picks one\\n860: // in a reservoir sampling manner from the nodes that had the highest score.\\n861: // It also returns the top {count} Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\\n864: \\tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\\n865: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\\n866: \\t}\\n867: \\n868: \\tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\\n869: \\theap.Init(&h)\\n870: 0, count)\\n874: \\tsortedNodeScoreList = append(sortedNodeScoreList, heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores))\\n875: \\n876: \\t// This for-loop will continue until all Nodes with the highest scores get checked for a reservoir sampling,\\n877: \\t// and sortedNodeScoreList gets (count - 1) elements.\\n878: \\tfor ns := heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores); ; ns = \\n883: \\t\\tif ns.TotalScore == sortedNodeScoreList[0].TotalScore {\\n884: \\t\\t\\tcntOfMaxScore++\\n885: \\t\\t\\tif rand.Intn(cntOfMaxScore) == 0 {\\n886: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Replace the candidate framework.NodeToStatusMap{scheduleResult.SuggestedHost: runPermitStatus},\n245: \t\t\t\t},\n246: \t\t\t}\n247: \t\t\tfitErr.Diagnosis.AddPluginStatus(runPermitStatus)\n248: \t\t\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, framework.NewStatus(runPermitStatus.Code()).WithError(fitErr)\n249: \t\t}\n250: \n251: \t\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, runPermitStatus\n252: \t}\n253: \n254: \t// At the end of a successful scheduling cycle, pop and move up Pods if needed.\n255: \tif len(podsToActivate.Map) != 0 {\n256: \t\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Activate(logger, podsToActivate.Map)\n257: \t\t// Clear the entries after activation.\n258: \t\tpodsToActivate.Map = make(map[string]*v1.Pod)\n259: \t}\n260: \n261: \treturn scheduleResult, assumedPodInfo, nil\n262: }\n263: \n264: // bindingCycle tries to bind an assumed Pod.\n265: func (sched *Scheduler) bindingCycle(\n266: \tctx context.Context,\n267: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n268: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n269: \tscheduleResult ScheduleResult,\n270: \tassumedPodInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo,\n271: \tstart time.Time,\n272: \tpodsToActivate *framework.PodsToActivate) *framework.Status {\n273: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n274: \n275: \tassumedPod := assumedPodInfo.Pod\n276: \n277: \t// Run \"permit\" plugins.\n278: \tif status := fwk.WaitOnPermit(ctx, assumedPod); !status.IsSuccess() {\n279: \t\tif status.IsRejected() {\n280: \t\t\tfitErr := &framework.FitError{\n281: \t\t\t\tNumAllNodes: 1,\n282: \t\t\t\tPod:         assumedPodInfo.Pod,\n283: \t\t\t\tDiagnosis: framework.Diagnosis{\n284: \t\t\t\t\tNodeToStatusMap:      framework.NodeToStatusMap{scheduleResult.SuggestedHost: status},\n285: \t\t\t\t\tUnschedulablePlugins: sets.New(status.Plugin()),\n286: \t\t\t\t},\n287: \t\t\t}\n288: \t\t\treturn framework.NewStatus(status.Code()).WithError(fitErr)\n289: \t\t}\n290: \t\treturn \t}\n302: \n303: \t// Calculating nodeResourceString can be heavy. Avoid it if klog verbosity is below 2.\n304: \tlogger.V(2).Info(\"Successfully bound pod to node\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(assumedPod), \"node\", scheduleResult.SuggestedHost, \"evaluatedNodes\", scheduleResult.EvaluatedNodes, \"feasibleNodes\", scheduleResult.FeasibleNodes)\n305: \tmetrics.PodScheduled(fwk.ProfileName(), metrics.SinceInSeconds(start))\n306: \tmetrics.PodSchedulingAttempts.Observe(float64(assumedPodInfo.Attempts))\n307: \tif assumedPodInfo.InitialAttemptTimestamp != nil {\n308: \t\tmetrics.PodSchedulingDuration.WithLabelValues(getAttemptsLabel(assumedPodInfo)).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(*assumedPodInfo.InitialAttemptTimestamp))\n309: \t\tmetrics.PodSchedulingSLIDuration.WithLabelValues(getAttemptsLabel(assumedPodInfo)).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(*assumedPodInfo.InitialAttemptTimestamp))\n310: \t}\n311: \t// Run \"postbind\" plugins.\n312: \tfwk.RunPostBindPlugins(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n313: \n314: \t// At the end of a successful binding cycle, move up Pods if needed.\n315: \tif len(podsToActivate.Map) != 0 {\n316: \t\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Activate(logger, podsToActivate.Map)\n317: \t\t// Unlike the logic in schedulingCycle(), we don't bother deleting the entries\n318: \t\t// as `podsToActivate.Map` is no longer consumed.\n319: \t}\n320: \n321: \treturn nil\n322: }\n323: \n324: func (sched *Scheduler) handleBindingCycleError(\n325: \tctx context.Context,\n326: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n327: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n328: \tpodInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo,\n329: \tstart time.Time,\n330: \tscheduleResult ScheduleResult,\n331: \tstatus *framework.Status) {\n332: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n333: \n334: \tassumedPod := podInfo.Pod\n335: \t// trigger un-reserve plugins to clean up state associated with the reserved Pod\n336: \tfwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n337: \tif forgetErr := sched.Cache.ForgetPod(logger, assumedPod); forgetErr != nil {\n338: \t\tlogger.Error(forgetErr, \"scheduler cache ForgetPod failed\")\n339: \t} else {\n340: \t\t// \"Forget\"ing an assumed Pod in binding cycle should be treated as a PodDelete event,\n341: \t\t// as the assumed Pod had occupied a certain amount of resources in scheduler cache.\n342: \t\t//\n343: \t\t// Avoid moving the assumed Pod itself as it's always Unschedulable.\n344: \t\t// It's intentional to \"defer\" this operation; otherwise MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue() would\n345: \t\t// add this event to in-flight events and thus move the assumed pod to backoffQ anyways if the plugins don't have appropriate QueueingHint.\n346: \t\tif status.IsRejected() {\n347: \t\t\tdefer sched.SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue(logger, internalqueue.AssignedPodDelete, assumedPod, nil, func(pod *v1.Pod) bool {\n348: \t\t\t\treturn assumedPod.UID != pod.UID\n349: \t\t\t})\n350: \t\t} else {\n351: \t\t\tsched.SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue(logger, internalqueue.AssignedPodDelete, assumedPod, nil, nil)\n352: \t\t}\n353: \t}\n354: \n355: \tsched.FailureHandler(ctx, fwk, podInfo, status, clearNominatedNode, start)\n356: }\n357: \n358: func (sched *Scheduler) frameworkForPod(pod *v1.Pod) (framework.Framework, error) {\n359: \tfwk, ok := sched.Profiles[pod.Spec.SchedulerName]\n360: \tif !ok {\n361: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"profile not found for scheduler name %q\", pod.Spec.SchedulerName)\n362: \t}\n363: \treturn fwk, nil\n364: }\n365: \n366: // skipPodSchedule returns true if we could skip scheduling the pod for specified cases.\n367: func (sched *Scheduler) skipPodSchedule(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, pod *v1.Pod) bool {\n368: \t// Case 1: pod is being deleted.\n369: \tif pod.DeletionTimestamp != nil {\n370: node list.\n388: // If it succeeds, it will return the name of the node.\n389: // If it fails, it will return a FitError with reasons.\n390: func (sched *Scheduler) schedulePod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) (result ScheduleResult, err error) {\n391: \ttrace := utiltrace.New(\"Scheduling\", utiltrace.Field{Key: \"namespace\", Value: pod.Namespace}, utiltrace.Field{Key: \"name\", Value: pod.Name})\n392: \tdefer trace.LogIfLong(100 * time.Millisecond)\n393: \tif err := sched.Cache.UpdateSnapshot(klog.FromContext(ctx), sched.nodeInfoSnapshot); err != nil {\n394: \t\treturn result, err\n395: \t}\n396: \ttrace.Step(\"Snapshotting scheduler cache and node infos done\")\n397: \n398: \tif \tif err != nil {\n404: \t\treturn result, err\n405: \t}\n406: \ttrace.Step(\"Computing predicates done\")\n407: \n408: \tif len(feasibleNodes) == 0 {\n409: \t\treturn result, &framework.FitError{\n410: \t\t\tPod:         pod,\n411: \t\t\tNumAllNodes: sched.nodeInfoSnapshot.NumNodes(),\n412: \t\t\tDiagnosis:   diagnosis,\n413: \t\t}\n414: \t}\n415: \n416: \t// When only one \t\tFeasibleNodes:  len(feasibleNodes),\n437: \t}, err\n438: }\n439: \n440: // Filters the nodes to find the ones that fit the pod based on the framework\n441: // filter plugins and filter extenders.\n442: func (sched *Scheduler) findNodesThatFitPod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, framework.Diagnosis, error) {\n443: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n444: \tdiagnosis := framework.Diagnosis{\n445: \t\tNodeToStatusMap: make(framework.NodeToStatusMap),\n446: \t}\n447: \n448: \tallNodes, err := sched.nodeInfoSnapshot.NodeInfos().List()\n449: \tif err != nil {\n450: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, err\n451: \t}\n452: \t// Run \"prefilter\" plugins.\n453: \tpreRes, s := fwk.RunPreFilterPlugins(ctx, state, pod)\n454: \tif !s.IsSuccess() {\n455: \t\tif !s.IsRejected() {\n456: \t\t\treturn nil, diagnosis, s.AsError()\n457: \t\t}\n458: \t\t// All nodes in NodeToStatusMap will have the same status so that they can be handled in the preemption.\n459: \t\t// Some non trivial refactoring is needed to avoid this copy.\n460: \t\tfor _, n := range allNodes {\n461: \t\t\tdiagnosis.NodeToStatusMap[n.Node().Name] = s\n462: \t\t}\n463: \n464: \t\t// Record the messages from PreFilter in Diagnosis.PreFilterMsg.\n465: \t\tmsg := s.Message()\n466: \t\tdiagnosis.PreFilterMsg = msg\n467: \t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Status after running PreFilter plugins for pod\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"status\", msg)\n468: \t\tdiagnosis.AddPluginStatus(s)\n469: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, nil\n470: \t}\n471: \n472: \t// \"NominatedNodeName\" can potentially be set in a previous scheduling cycle as a result of preemption.\n473: \t// This node is likely the only candidate that will fit the pod, and hence we try it first before iterating over all nodes.\n474: \tif len(pod.Status.NominatedNodeName) > 0 {\n475: \t\tfeasibleNodes, err := sched.evaluateNominatedNode(ctx, pod, fwk, state, diagnosis)\n476: \t\tif err != nil {\n477: \t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Evaluation failed on nominated node\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"node\", pod.Status.NominatedNodeName)\n478: \t\t}\n479: \t\t// Nominated node passes all the filters, scheduler is good to assign this node to the pod.\n480: \t\tif len(feasibleNodes) != 0 {\n481: \t\t\treturn feasibleNodes, diagnosis, nil\n482: \t\t}\n483: \t}\n484: \n485: \tnodes := allNodes\n486: \tif !preRes.AllNodes() {\n487: \t\tnodes = make([]*framework.NodeInfo, 0, len(preRes.NodeNames))\n488: \t\tfor _, n := range allNodes {\n489: \t\t\tif !preRes.NodeNames.Has(n.Node().Name) {\n490: \t\t\t\t// We consider Nodes that are filtered out by PreFilterResult as rejected via UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n491: \t\t\t\t// We have to record them in NodeToStatusMap so that they won't be considered as candidates in the preemption.\n492: \t\t\t\tdiagnosis.NodeToStatusMap[n.Node().Name] = framework.NewStatus(framework.UnschedulableAndUnresolvable, \"node is filtered out by the prefilter result\")\n493: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n494: \t\t\t}\n495: \t\t\tnodes = append(nodes, n)\n496: \t\t}\n497: \t}\n498: \tfeasibleNodes, err := sched.findNodesThatPassFilters(ctx, fwk, state, pod, &diagnosis, nodes)\n499: \t// always try to update the sched.nextStartNodeIndex regardless of whether an error has occurred\n500: \t// this is helpful to make sure that all the nodes have a chance to be searched\n501: \tprocessedNodes := len(feasibleNodes) + len(diagnosis.NodeToStatusMap)\n502: \tsched.nextStartNodeIndex = (sched.nextStartNodeIndex + processedNodes) % len(nodes)\n503: \tif err != nil {\n504: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, err\n505: \t}\n506: \n507: \tfeasibleNodesAfterExtender, err := findNodesThatPassExtenders(ctx, sched.Extenders, pod, feasibleNodes, diagnosis.NodeToStatusMap)\n508: \tif err != nil {\n509: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, err\n510: \t}\n511: \tif len(feasibleNodesAfterExtender) != len(feasibleNodes) {\n512: \t\t// Extenders filtered out some nodes.\n513: \t\t//\n514: \t\t// Extender doesn't support any kind of requeueing feature like EnqueueExtensions in the scheduling framework.\n515: \t\t// When Extenders reject some Nodes and the pod ends up being unschedulable,\n516: \t\t// we put framework.ExtenderName to pInfo.UnschedulablePlugins.\n517: \t\t// This Pod will be requeued from unschedulable pod pool to activeQ/backoffQ\n518: \t\t// by any kind of cluster events.\n519: \t\t// https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/122019\n520: \t\tif diagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins == nil {\n521: \t\t\tdiagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins = sets.New[string]()\n522: \t\t}\n523: \t\tdiagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins.Insert(framework.ExtenderName)\n524: \t}\n525: \n526: \treturn feasibleNodesAfterExtender, diagnosis, nil\n527: }\n528: \n529: func (sched *Scheduler) evaluateNominatedNode(ctx context.Context, pod *v1.Pod, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, diagnosis framework.Diagnosis) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n530: \tnnn := nil\n547: }\n548: \n549: // hasScoring checks if scoring nodes is configured.\n550: func (sched *Scheduler) hasScoring(fwk framework.Framework) bool {\n551: \tif fwk.HasScorePlugins() {\n552: \n562: // hasExtenderFilters checks if any extenders filter nodes.\n563: func (sched *Scheduler) hasExtenderFilters() bool {\n564: \tfor _, extender := range sched.Extenders {\n565: \t\tif *Scheduler) findNodesThatPassFilters(\n574: \tctx context.Context,\n575: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n576: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n577: \tpod *v1.Pod,\n578: \tdiagnosis *framework.Diagnosis,\n579: \tnodes []*framework.NodeInfo) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n580: \tnumAllNodes := len(nodes)\n581: \tnumNodesToFind := sched.numFeasibleNodesToFind(fwk.PercentageOfNodesToScore(), int32(numAllNodes))\n582: \tif !sched.hasExtenderFilters() && !sched.hasScoring(fwk) {\n583: \t\tnumNodesToFind = 1\n584: \t}\n585: \n586: \t// Create feasible list with enough space to avoid growing it\n587: \t// and allow assigning.\n588: \tfeasibleNodes := make([]*framework.NodeInfo, numNodesToFind)\n589: \n590: \tif \t}\n596: \n597: \terrCh := parallelize.NewErrorChannel()\n598: \tvar feasibleNodesLen int32\n599: \tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n600: \tdefer cancel()\n601: \n602: \ttype nodeStatus struct {\n603: \t\tnode   string\n604: \t\tstatus *framework.Status\n605: \t}\n606: \tresult := make([]*nodeStatus, numAllNodes)\n607: \tcheckNode := func(i int) {\n608: \t\t// We check the nodes starting from where we left off in the previous scheduling cycle,\n609: \t\t// this is to make sure all nodes have the same chance of being examined across pods.\n610: \t\tnodeInfo := \t\t\terrCh.SendErrorWithCancel(status.AsError(), cancel)\n614: \t\t\treturn\n615: \t\t}\n616: \t\tif status.IsSuccess() {\n617: \t\t\tlength := atomic.AddInt32(&feasibleNodesLen, 1)\n618: \t\t\tif length > numNodesToFind {\n619: \t\t\t\tcancel()\n620: \t\t\t\tatomic.AddInt32(&feasibleNodesLen, -1)\n621: \t\t\t} else {\n622: \t\t\t\tfeasibleNodes[length-1] = nodeInfo\n623: \t\t\t}\n624: \t\t} else {\n625: \t\t\tresult[i] = &nodeStatus{node: nodeInfo.Node().Name, status: status}\n626: \t\t}\n627: \t}\n628: \n629: \tbeginCheckNode := time.Now()\n630: \tstatusCode := framework.Success\n631: \tdefer func() {\n632: \t\t// We record Filter extension point latency here instead of in framework.go because framework.RunFilterPlugins\n633: \t\t// function is called for each node, whereas we want to have an overall latency for all nodes per scheduling cycle.\n634: \t\t// Note that this latency also includes latency for `addNominatedPods`, which calls framework.RunPreFilterAddPod.\n635: \t\tmetrics.FrameworkExtensionPointDuration.WithLabelValues(metrics.Filter, statusCode.String(), fwk.ProfileName()).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(beginCheckNode))\n636: \t}()\n637: \n638: \t// Stops searching for more nodes once the configured number of feasible nodes\n639: \t// are found.\n640: \tfwk.Parallelizer().Until(ctx, numAllNodes, checkNode, metrics.Filter)\n641: \tfeasibleNodes = feasibleNodes[:feasibleNodesLen]\n642: \tfor _, item := range result {\n643: \t\tif item == nil {\n644: \t\t\tcontinue\n645: \t\t}\n646: \t\tdiagnosis.NodeToStatusMap[item.node] = item.status\n647: \treturn feasibleNodes, nil\n654: }\n655: \n656: // numFeasibleNodesToFind returns the number of feasible nodes that once found, the scheduler stops\n657: // its search for more feasible nodes.\n658: func (sched *Scheduler) numFeasibleNodesToFind(percentageOfNodesToScore *int32, numAllNodes int32) (numNodes int32) {\n659: \tif numAllNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n660: \t\treturn numAllNodes\n661: \t}\n662: \n663: \t// Use profile percentageOfNodesToScore if it's set. Otherwise, use global percentageOfNodesToScore.\n664: \tvar percentage int32\n665: \tif percentageOfNodesToScore != nil {\n666: \t\tpercentage = *percentageOfNodesToScore\n667: \t} else {\n668: \t\tpercentage = sched.percentageOfNodesToScore\n669: \t}\n670: \n671: \tif percentage == 0 {\n672: \t\tpercentage = int32(50) - numAllNodes/125\n673: \t\tif percentage < minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind {\n674: \t\t\tpercentage = minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind\n675: \t\t}\n676: \t}\n677: \n678: \tnumNodes = numAllNodes * percentage / 100\n679: \tif numNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n680: \t\treturn minFeasibleNodesToFind\n681: \t}\n682: \n683: \treturn numNodes\n684: }\n685: \n686: func findNodesThatPassExtenders(ctx context.Context, extenders []framework.Extender, pod *v1.Pod, feasibleNodes []*framework.NodeInfo, statuses framework.NodeToStatusMap) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n687: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n688: \t// Extenders are called sequentially.\n689: \t// Nodes in original feasibleNodes can be excluded in one extender, and pass on to the next\n690: \t// extender in a decreasing manner.\n691: \tfor _, extender := range extenders {\n692: \t\tif len(feasibleNodes) == 0 {\n693: \t\t\tbreak\n694: \t\t}\n695: \t\tif !extender.IsInterested(pod) {\n696: \t\t\tcontinue\n697: \t\t}\n698: \n699: \t\t// Status of failed nodes in failedAndUnresolvableMap will be added or overwritten in <statuses>,\n700: \t\t// so that the scheduler framework can respect the UnschedulableAndUnresolvable status for\n701: \t\t// particular nodes, and this may eventually improve preemption efficiency.\n702: \t\t// Note: users are recommended to configure the extenders that may return UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n703: \t\t// status ahead of others.\n704: \t\tfeasibleList, failedMap, failedAndUnresolvableMap, err := extender.Filter(pod, feasibleNodes)\n705: \t\tif err != nil {\n706: \t\t\tif extender.IsIgnorable() {\n707: \t\t\t\tlogger.Info(\"Skipping extender as it returned error and has ignorable flag set\", \"extender\", extender, \"err\", err)\n708: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n709: \t\t\t}\n710: \t\t\treturn nil, err\n711: \t\t}\n712: \n713: \t\tfor failedNodeName, failedMsg := range failedAndUnresolvableMap {\n714: \t\t\tvar aggregatedReasons []string\n715: \t\t\tif _, found := statuses[failedNodeName]; found {\n716: \t\t\t\taggregatedReasons = statuses[failedNodeName].Reasons()\n717: \t\t\t}\n718: \t\t\taggregatedReasons = append(aggregatedReasons, failedMsg)\n719: \t\t\tstatuses[failedNodeName] = framework.NewStatus(framework.UnschedulableAndUnresolvable, aggregatedReasons...)\n720: \t\t}\n721: \n722: \t\tfor \\n859: // selectHost takes a prioritized list of nodes and then picks one\\n860: // in a reservoir sampling manner from the nodes that had the highest score.\\n861: // It also returns the top {count} Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\\n864: \\tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\\n865: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\\n866: \\t}\\n867: \\n868: \\tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\\n869: \\theap.Init(&h)\\n870: 0, count)\\n874: \\tsortedNodeScoreList = append(sortedNodeScoreList, heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores))\\n875: \\n876: \\t// This for-loop will continue until all Nodes with the highest scores get checked for a reservoir sampling,\\n877: \\t// and sortedNodeScoreList gets (count - 1) elements.\\n878: \\tfor ns := heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores); ; ns = \\n883: \\t\\tif ns.TotalScore == sortedNodeScoreList[0].TotalScore {\\n884: \\t\\t\\tcntOfMaxScore++\\n885: \\t\\t\\tif rand.Intn(cntOfMaxScore) == 0 {\\n886: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Replace the candidate n-1]\\n931: \\treturn x\\n932: }\\n933: \\n934: // assume signals to the cache that a pod is already in the cache, so that binding can be asynchronous.\\n935: // assume modifies `assumed`.\\n936: func \\\"k8s.io/kubernetes/pkg/scheduler/util\\\"\\n39: )\\n40: \\n41: var generation int64\\n42: \\n43: // ActionType is an integer to represent one type of resource change.\\n44: // Different ActionTypes can be bit-wised to compose new semantics.\\n45: type ActionType int64\\n46: \\n47: // Constants for ActionTypes.\\n48: const (\\n49: \\tAdd    ActionType = 1 << iota // 1\\n50: \\tDelete                        // 10\\n51: \\t// UpdateNodeXYZ is only applicable for Node events.\\n52: \\tUpdateNodeAllocatable // 100\\n53: \\tUpdateNodeLabel       // 1000\\n54: \\tUpdateNodeTaint       // 10000\\n55: \\tUpdateNodeCondition   // 100000\\n56: \\tUpdateNodeAnnotation  // 1000000\\n57: \\n58: \\tAll ActionType = 1<<iota - 1 // 1111111\\n59: \\n60: \\t// Use the general Update type if you don't either know or care the specific sub-Update type to use.\\n61: \\tUpdate = UpdateNodeAllocatable | UpdateNodeLabel | UpdateNodeTaint | UpdateNodeCondition | UpdateNodeAnnotation\\n62: )\\n63: \\n64: // GVK is short for group/version/kind, which can uniquely represent a particular API resource.\\n65: type GVK string\\n66: \\n67: // Constants for GVKs.\\n68: const (\\n69: \\t// There are a couple of notes about how the scheduler notifies the events of Pods:\\n70: \\t// - Add: add events could be triggered by either a newly created Pod or an existing Pod that is scheduled to a Node.\\n71: \\t// - Delete: delete events could be triggered by:\\n72: \\t//           - a Pod that is deleted\\n73: \\t//           - a Pod that was assumed, but gets un-assumed due to some errors in the binding cycle.\\n74: \\t//           - an existing Pod that was unscheduled but gets scheduled to a Node.\\n75: \\tPod GVK = \\\"Pod\\\"\\n76: \\t// A note about NodeAdd event and UpdateNodeTaint event:\\n77: \\t// NodeAdd QueueingHint isn't always called because of the internal feature called preCheck.\\n78: \\t// It's definitely not something expected for plugin developers,\\n79: \\t// and registering UpdateNodeTaint event is the only mitigation for now.\\n80: \\t// So, kube-scheduler registers UpdateNodeTaint event for plugins that has NodeAdded event, but don't have UpdateNodeTaint event.\\n81: \\t// It has a bad impact for the requeuing efficiency though, a lot better than some Pods being stuck in the\\n82: \\t// unschedulable pod pool.\\n83: \\t// This behavior will be removed when we remove the preCheck feature.\\n84: \\t// See: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/110175\\n85: \\tNode                    GVK = \\\"Node\\\"\\n86: \\tPersistentVolume        GVK = \\\"PersistentVolume\\\"\\n87: \\tPersistentVolumeClaim   GVK = \\\"PersistentVolumeClaim\\\"\\n88: \\tCSINode                 GVK = \\\"storage.k8s.io/CSINode\\\"\\n89: \\tCSIDriver               GVK = \\\"storage.k8s.io/CSIDriver\\\"\\n90: \\tCSIStorageCapacity      GVK = \\\"storage.k8s.io/CSIStorageCapacity\\\"\\n91: \\tStorageClass            GVK = \\\"storage.k8s.io/StorageClass\\\"\\n92: \\tPodSchedulingContext    GVK = \\\"PodSchedulingContext\\\"\\n93: \\tResourceClaim           GVK = \\\"ResourceClaim\\\"\\n94: \\tResourceClass           GVK = \\\"ResourceClass\\\"\\n95: \\tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \\\"ResourceClaimParameters\\\"\\n96: \\tResourceClassParameters GVK = \\\"ResourceClassParameters\\\"\\n97: \\n98: \\t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\\n99: \\t// e.g., If you register `{Resource: \\\"*\\\", ActionType: All}` in EventsToRegister,\\n100: \\t// all coming clusterEvents will be admitted. Be careful to register it, it will\\n101: \\t// increase the computing pressure in requeueing unless you really need it.\\n102: \\t//\\n103: \\t// Meanwhile, if the coming clusterEvent is a wildcard one, all pods\\n104: \\t// will be moved from unschedulablePod pool to activeQ/backoffQ forcibly.\\n105: \\tWildCard GVK = \\\"*\\\"\\n106: )\\n107: \\n108: type ClusterEventWithHint struct {\\n109: \\tEvent ClusterEvent\\n110: \\t// QueueingHintFn is executed for the plugin rejected by this plugin when the above Event happens,\\n111: \\t// and filters out events to reduce useless retry of Pod's scheduling.\\n112: \\t// It's an optional field. If not set,\\n113: \\t// the scheduling of Pods will be always retried with backoff when this Event happens.\\n114: \\t// (the same as Queue)\\n115: \\tQueueingHintFn QueueingHintFn\\n116: }\\n117: \\n118: // QueueingHintFn returns a hint that signals whether the event can make a Pod,\\n119: // which was rejected by this plugin in the past scheduling cycle, schedulable or not.\\n120: // It's called before a Pod gets moved from unschedulableQ to backoffQ or activeQ.\\n121: // If it returns an error, we'll take the returned QueueingHint as `Queue` at the caller whatever we returned here so that\\n122: // we can prevent the Pod from being stuck in the unschedulable pod pool.\\n123: //\\n124: // - `pod`: the Pod to be enqueued, which is rejected by this plugin in the past.\\n125: // - `oldObj` `newObj`: the object involved in that event.\\n126: //   - For example, the given event is \\\"Node deleted\\\", the `oldObj` will be that deleted Node.\\n127: //   - `oldObj` is nil if the event is add event.\\n128: //   - `newObj` is nil if the event is delete event.\\n129: type QueueingHintFn func(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod, oldObj, newObj interface{}) (QueueingHint, error)\\n130: \\n131: type QueueingHint int\\n132: \\n133: const (\\n134: \\t// QueueSkip implies that the cluster event has no impact on\\n135: \\t// scheduling of the pod.\\n136: \\tQueueSkip QueueingHint = iota\\n137: \\n138: \\t// Queue implies that the Pod may be schedulable by the event.\\n139: \\tQueue\\n140: )\\n141: \\n142: func (s QueueingHint) String() string {\\n143: \\tswitch s {\\n144: \\tcase QueueSkip:\\n145: \\t\\treturn \\\"QueueSkip\\\"\\n146: \\tcase Queue:\\n147: \\t\\treturn \\\"Queue\\\"\\n148: \\t}\\n149: \\treturn \\\"\\\"\\n150: }\\n151: \\n152: // ClusterEvent abstracts how a system resource's state gets changed.\\n153: // Resource represents the standard API resources such as Pod, Node, etc.\\n154: // ActionType denotes the specific change such as Add, Update or Delete.\\n155: type ClusterEvent struct {\\n156: \\tResource   GVK\\n157: \\tActionType ActionType\\n158: \\tLabel      string\\n159: }\\n160: \\n161: // IsWildCard returns true if ClusterEvent follows WildCard semantics\\n162: func (ce ClusterEvent) IsWildCard() bool {\\n163: \\treturn ce.Resource == WildCard && ce.ActionType == All\\n164: }\\n165: \\n166: // Match returns true CheckConflict(ip, protocol string, port int32) bool {\\n1035: \\tif port <= 0 {\\n1036: \\t\\treturn false\\n1037: \\t}\\n1038: \\n1039: \\th.sanitize(&ip, &protocol)\\n1040: \\n1041: \\tpp := \"k8s.io/kubernetes/pkg/scheduler/util\"\n39: )\n40: \n41: var generation int64\n42: \n43: // ActionType is an integer to represent one type of resource change.\n44: // Different ActionTypes can be bit-wised to compose new semantics.\n45: type ActionType int64\n46: \n47: // Constants for ActionTypes.\n48: const (\n49: \tAdd    ActionType = 1 << iota // 1\n50: \tDelete                        // 10\n51: \t// UpdateNodeXYZ is only applicable for Node events.\n52: \tUpdateNodeAllocatable // 100\n53: \tUpdateNodeLabel       // 1000\n54: \tUpdateNodeTaint       // 10000\n55: \tUpdateNodeCondition   // 100000\n56: \tUpdateNodeAnnotation  // 1000000\n57: \n58: \tAll ActionType = 1<<iota - 1 // 1111111\n59: \n60: \t// Use the general Update type if you don't either know or care the specific sub-Update type to use.\n61: \tUpdate = UpdateNodeAllocatable | UpdateNodeLabel | UpdateNodeTaint | UpdateNodeCondition | UpdateNodeAnnotation\n62: )\n63: \n64: // GVK is short for group/version/kind, which can uniquely represent a particular API resource.\n65: type GVK string\n66: \n67: // Constants for GVKs.\n68: const (\n69: \t// There are a couple of notes about how the scheduler notifies the events of Pods:\n70: \t// - Add: add events could be triggered by either a newly created Pod or an existing Pod that is scheduled to a Node.\n71: \t// - Delete: delete events could be triggered by:\n72: \t//           - a Pod that is deleted\n73: \t//           - a Pod that was assumed, but gets un-assumed due to some errors in the binding cycle.\n74: \t//           - an existing Pod that was unscheduled but gets scheduled to a Node.\n75: \tPod GVK = \"Pod\"\n76: \t// A note about NodeAdd event and UpdateNodeTaint event:\n77: \t// NodeAdd QueueingHint isn't always called because of the internal feature called preCheck.\n78: \t// It's definitely not something expected for plugin developers,\n79: \t// and registering UpdateNodeTaint event is the only mitigation for now.\n80: \t// So, kube-scheduler registers UpdateNodeTaint event for plugins that has NodeAdded event, but don't have UpdateNodeTaint event.\n81: \t// It has a bad impact for the requeuing efficiency though, a lot better than some Pods being stuck in the\n82: \t// unschedulable pod pool.\n83: \t// This behavior will be removed when we remove the preCheck feature.\n84: \t// See: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/110175\n85: \tNode                    GVK = \"Node\"\n86: \tPersistentVolume        GVK = \"PersistentVolume\"\n87: \tPersistentVolumeClaim   GVK = \"PersistentVolumeClaim\"\n88: \tCSINode                 GVK = \"storage.k8s.io/CSINode\"\n89: \tCSIDriver               GVK = \"storage.k8s.io/CSIDriver\"\n90: \tCSIStorageCapacity      GVK = \"storage.k8s.io/CSIStorageCapacity\"\n91: \tStorageClass            GVK = \"storage.k8s.io/StorageClass\"\n92: \tPodSchedulingContext    GVK = \"PodSchedulingContext\"\n93: \tResourceClaim           GVK = \"ResourceClaim\"\n94: \tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n95: \tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n96: \tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n97: \n98: \t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n99: \t// e.g., If you register `{Resource: \"*\", ActionType: All}` in EventsToRegister,\n100: \t// all coming clusterEvents will be admitted. Be careful to register it, it will\n101: \t// increase the computing pressure in requeueing unless you really need it.\n102: \t//\n103: \t// Meanwhile, if the coming clusterEvent is a wildcard one, all pods\n104: \t// will be moved from unschedulablePod pool to activeQ/backoffQ forcibly.\n105: \tWildCard GVK = \"*\"\n106: )\n107: \n108: type ClusterEventWithHint struct {\n109: \tEvent ClusterEvent\n110: \t// QueueingHintFn is executed for the plugin rejected by this plugin when the above Event happens,\n111: \t// and filters out events to reduce useless retry of Pod's scheduling.\n112: \t// It's an optional field. If not set,\n113: \t// the scheduling of Pods will be always retried with backoff when this Event happens.\n114: \t// (the same as Queue)\n115: \tQueueingHintFn QueueingHintFn\n116: }\n117: \n118: // QueueingHintFn returns a hint that signals whether the event can make a Pod,\n119: // which was rejected by this plugin in the past scheduling cycle, schedulable or not.\n120: // It's called before a Pod gets moved from unschedulableQ to backoffQ or activeQ.\n121: // If it returns an error, we'll take the returned QueueingHint as `Queue` at the caller whatever we returned here so that\n122: // we can prevent the Pod from being stuck in the unschedulable pod pool.\n123: //\n124: // - `pod`: the Pod to be enqueued, which is rejected by this plugin in the past.\n125: // - `oldObj` `newObj`: the object involved in that event.\n126: //   - For example, the given event is \"Node deleted\", the `oldObj` will be that deleted Node.\n127: //   - `oldObj` is nil if the event is add event.\n128: //   - `newObj` is nil if the event is delete event.\n129: type QueueingHintFn func(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod, oldObj, newObj interface{}) (QueueingHint, error)\n130: \n131: type QueueingHint int\n132: \n133: const (\n134: \t// QueueSkip implies that the cluster event has no impact on\n135: \t// scheduling of the pod.\n136: \tQueueSkip QueueingHint = iota\n137: \n138: \t// Queue implies that the Pod may be schedulable by the event.\n139: \tQueue\n140: )\n141: \n142: func (s QueueingHint) String() string {\n143: \tswitch s {\n144: \tcase QueueSkip:\n145: \t\treturn \"QueueSkip\"\n146: \tcase Queue:\n147: \t\treturn \"Queue\"\n148: \t}\n149: \treturn \"\"\n150: }\n151: \n152: // ClusterEvent abstracts how a system resource's state gets changed.\n153: // Resource represents the ce.Resource == WildCard && ce.ActionType == All\n164: }\n165: \n166: // Match returns true if ClusterEvent is matched with the coming event.\n167: // If the ce.Resource is \"*\", there's no requirement for the coming event' Resource.\n168: // Contrarily, if the coming event's Resource is \"*\", the ce.Resource should only be \"*\".\n169: //\n170: // Note: we have a special case here when fmt.Sprintf(NoNodeAvailableMsg+\":\", f.NumAllNodes)\n376: \tpreFilterMsg := f.Diagnosis.PreFilterMsg\n377: \tif preFilterMsg != \"\" {\n378: \t\t// PreFilter plugin returns unschedulable.\n379: \t\t// Add the messages from PreFilter plugins to reasonMsg.\n380: \t\treasonMsg += fmt.Sprintf(\" %v.\", preFilterMsg)\n381: \t}\n382: \n383: \tif preFilterMsg == \"\" {\n384: \t\t// the scheduling Resource.\n664: func (r *Resource) SetMaxResource(rl v1.ResourceList) {\n665: \tif r == nil {\n666: \t\treturn\n667: \t}\n668: \n669: \tfor rName, rQuantity := range rl {\n670: \t\tswitch rName \n779: // AddPod is a wrapper around AddPodInfo.\n780: func (n *NodeInfo) AddPod(pod *v1.Pod) {\n781: \t// ignore this err since apiserver doesn't properly validate affinity terms\n782: \t// and we }\n797: \n798: func removeFromSlice(logger klog.Logger, s []*PodInfo, k string) ([]*PodInfo, bool) {\n799: \tvar removed bool\n800: \tfor i := range s {\n801: \t\ttmpKey, err := GetPodKey(s[i].Pod)\n802: \t\tif err != nil {\n803: \t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Cannot get pod key\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(s[i].Pod))\n804: \t\t\tcontinue\n805: \t\t}\n806: \t\tif k == tmpKey {\n807: \t\t\t// delete the element\n808: \t\t\ts[i] = s[len(s)-1]\n809: \t\t\ts = s[:len(s)-1]\n810: \t\t\tremoved = true\n811: \t\t\tbreak\n812: \t\t}\n813: \t}\n814: \t// resets the slices to nil so that we can do DeepEqual in unit tests.\n815: \tif len(s) == 0 {\n816: \t\treturn nil, removed\n817: \t}\n818: \treturn s, removed\n819: }\n820: \n821: // RemovePod subtracts pod information from this // update node info based on the pod and sign.\n843: // The sign will be set to `+1` when AddPod and to `-1` when RemovePod.\n844: func (n *NodeInfo) update(pod *v1.Pod, sign int64) {\n845: \tres, non0CPU, non0Mem := calculateResource(pod)\n846: \tn.Requested.MilliCPU += sign * res.MilliCPU\n847: \tn.Requested.Memory += sign * res.Memory\n848: \tn.Requested.EphemeralStorage += sign * res.EphemeralStorage\n849: \tif n.Requested.ScalarResources == nil && len(res.ScalarResources) > 0 {\n850: \t\tn.Requested.ScalarResources = map[v1.ResourceName]int64{}\n851: \t}\n852: \tfor rName, rQuant := range res.ScalarResources {\n853: \t\tn.Requested.ScalarResources[rName] += sign * rQuant\n854: \t}\n855: \tn.NonZeroRequested.MilliCPU += sign * non0CPU\n856: \tn.NonZeroRequested.Memory += sign * non0Mem\n857: \n858: \t// Consume ports when pod added or release ports when pod removed.\n859: \tn.updateUsedPorts(pod, sign > 0)\n860: \tn.updatePVCRefCounts(pod, sign > 0)\n861: \n862: \tn.Generation = nextGeneration()\n863: }\n864: \n865: func calculateResource(pod *v1.Pod) (Resource, int64, int64) {\n866: \tvar non0InitCPU, non0InitMem int64\n867: \tvar non0CPU, non0Mem int64\n868: \trequests := resourcehelper.PodRequests(pod, resourcehelper.PodResourcesOptions{\n869: \t\tInPlacePodVerticalScalingEnabled: utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.InPlacePodVerticalScaling),\n870: \t\tContainerFn: func(requests v1.ResourceList, containerType podutil.ContainerType) {\n871: \t\t\tnon0CPUReq, non0MemReq := schedutil.GetNonzeroRequests(&requests)\n872: \t\t\tswitch containerType {\n873: \t\t\tcase podutil.Containers:\n874: \t\t\t\tnon0CPU += non0CPUReq\n875: \t\t\t\tnon0Mem += non0MemReq\n876: \t\t\tcase podutil.InitContainers:\n877: \t\t\t\tnon0InitCPU = max(non0InitCPU, non0CPUReq)\n878: \t\t\t\tnon0InitMem = max(non0InitMem, non0MemReq)\n879: \t\t\t}\n880: \t\t},\n881: \t})\n882: \n883: \tnon0CPU = max(non0CPU, non0InitCPU)\n884: \tnon0Mem = max(non0Mem, non0InitMem)\n885: \n886: \t// If Overhead is being utilized, add to the non-zero cpu/memory tracking for the pod. It has already been added\n887: \t// into ScalarResources since it is part of requests\n888: \tif pod.Spec.Overhead != nil {\n889: \t\tif _, found := pod.Spec.Overhead[v1.ResourceCPU]; found {\n890: \t\t\tnon0CPU += pod.Spec.Overhead.Cpu().MilliValue()\n891: \t\t}\n892: \n893: \t\tif _, found := pod.Spec.Overhead[v1.ResourceMemory]; found {\n894: \t\t\tnon0Mem += pod.Spec.Overhead.Memory().Value()\n895: \t\t}\n896: \t}\n897: \tvar res Resource\n898: \tres.Add(requests)\n899: \treturn res, non0CPU, non0Mem\n900: }\n901: \n902: // updateUsedPorts updates the UsedPorts of NodeInfo.\n903: func (n *NodeInfo) updateUsedPorts(pod *v1.Pod, add bool) {\n904: \tfor _, container := range pod.Spec.Containers {\n905: \t\tfor _, podPort := range container.Ports {\n906: \t\t\tif add {\n907: \t\t\t\tn.UsedPorts.Add(podPort.HostIP, string(podPort.Protocol), podPort.HostPort)\n908: \t\t\t} else {\n909: \t\t\t\tn.UsedPorts.Remove(podPort.HostIP, string(podPort.Protocol), podPort.HostPort)\n910: \t\t\t}\n911: \t\t}\n912: \t}\n913: }\n914: \n915: // updatePVCRefCounts updates the PVCRefCounts of NodeInfo.\n916: func (n *NodeInfo) updatePVCRefCounts(pod *v1.Pod, add bool) {\n917: \tfor _, v := range pod.Spec.Volumes {\n918: \t\tif v.PersistentVolumeClaim == nil {\n919: \t\t\tcontinue\n920: \t\t}\n921: \n922: \t\tkey := n.PVCRefCounts[key] <= 0 {\n928: \t\t\t\tdelete(n.PVCRefCounts, key)\n929: \t\t\t}\n930: \t\t}\n931: \t}\n932: }\n933: \n934: // SetNode sets the overall node information.\n935: func (n *NodeInfo) string {\n958: \treturn fmt.Sprintf(\"%s/%s\", namespace, name)\n959: }\n960: \n961: // DefaultBindAllHostIP defines the default ip address used to bind to all host.\n962: const DefaultBindAllHostIP = \"0.0.0.0\"\n963: \n964: // ProtocolPort represents a protocol port pair, e.g. tcp:80.\n965: type ProtocolPort struct {\n966: \tProtocol string\n967: \tPort     int32\n968: }\n969: \n970: // NewProtocolPort creates a ProtocolPort instance.\n971: func NewProtocolPort(protocol string, port int32) *ProtocolPort {\n972: \tpp := &ProtocolPort{\n973: \t\tProtocol: protocol,\n974: \t\tPort:     port,\n975: \t}\n976: \n977: \tif len(pp.Protocol) == 0 {\n978: \t\tpp.Protocol = string(v1.ProtocolTCP)\n979: \t}\n980: \n981: \treturn pp\n982: }\n983: \n984: // HostPortInfo stores mapping from ip to a set of ProtocolPort\n985: type HostPortInfo map[string]map[ProtocolPort]struct{}\n986: \n987: // Add adds (ip, protocol, port) to HostPortInfo\n988: func (h HostPortInfo) Add(ip, protocol string, port int32) {\n989: \tif port <= 0 {\n990: \t\treturn\n991: \t}\n992: \n993: \th.sanitize(&ip, &protocol)\n994: \n995: \tpp := NewProtocolPort(protocol, port)\n996: \tif _, ok := h[ip]; !ok {\n997: \t\th[ip] = map[ProtocolPort]struct{}{\n998: \t\t\t*pp: {},\n999: \t\t}\n1000: \t\treturn\n1001: \t}\n1002: \n1003: \th[ip][*pp] = struct{}{}\n1004: }\n1005: \n1006: // Remove removes (ip, protocol, port) from HostPortInfo\n1007: func (h HostPortInfo) Remove(ip, protocol string, port int32) {\n1008: \tif port <= 0 {\n1009: \t\treturn\n1010: \t}\n1011: \n1012: \th.sanitize(&ip, &protocol)\n1013: \n1014: \tpp := NewProtocolPort(protocol, port)\n1015: \tif m, ok := h[ip]; ok {\n1016: \t\tdelete(m, *pp)\n1017: \t\tif len(h[ip]) == 0 {\n1018: \t\t\tdelete(h, ip)\n1019: \t\t}\n1020: \t}\n1021: }\n1022: \n1023: // Len returns the total number of (ip, protocol, port) tuple in HostPortInfo\n1024: func (h HostPortInfo) Len() int {\n1025: \tlength := 0\n1026: \tfor _, m := range h {\n1027: \t\tlength += len(m)\n1028: \t}\n1029: \treturn length\n1030: }\n1031: \n1032: // CheckConflict checks if the input (ip, protocol, port) conflicts with the existing\n1033: // ones in HostPortInfo.\n1034: func (h HostPortInfo) CheckConflict(ip, protocol string, port int32) bool {\n1035: \tif port <= 0 {\n1036: \t\treturn false\n1037: \t}\n1038: \n1039: \th.sanitize(&ip,   "content": "# Kubernetes Scheduler ResourceSlice Event Handler Bug - Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n\n- `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` \u2014 Entry point for scheduling cycle; calls `ScheduleOne()` which invokes `schedulingCycle()` that calls `SchedulePod()`, which eventually checks resource allocation status\n- `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` \u2014 Registers event handlers for cluster resources; examined the `addAllEventHandlers()` function that sets up handlers for various resource types including Dynamic Resource Allocation resources\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` \u2014 Defines GVK (Group/Version/Kind) constants for all supported resource types and the `UnrollWildCardResource()` function\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` \u2014 DRA plugin that checks resource availability; examined the `EventsToRegister()` method that returns events that should trigger pod rescheduling\n- `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` \u2014 Scheduler initialization (referenced for context)\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/api/resource/v1alpha2/types.go` \u2014 ResourceSlice API type definition (confirmed it exists)\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:111` \u2014 `schedulingCycle()` calls `SchedulePod()` which executes the plugin chain\n2. **Plugin evaluation**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go:418-423` \u2014 `PreEnqueue()` checks if all resource claims can be allocated\n3. **Filter execution**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` \u2014 Filter phase checks if resources are available on nodes\n4. **Event registration**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go:381-413` \u2014 `EventsToRegister()` specifies which cluster events should trigger pod rescheduling\n5. **Event handler setup**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go:287-546` \u2014 `addAllEventHandlers()` registers informer handlers for cluster resource events\n6. **GVK definition missing**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go:64-106` \u2014 ResourceSlice is not defined as a framework GVK\n7. **Bug triggered**: When a ResourceSlice is created/updated after a pod fails scheduling, **no event handler exists to notify the scheduler queue**\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n**Function**: GVK constant definitions and `UnrollWildCardResource()`\n**Line**: ~92-106 and ~177-193\n**Explanation**:\n\nThe framework is missing a GVK constant for ResourceSlice. Although ResourceSlice objects exist in the Kubernetes API and are used by the DRA plugin to track available resources, they are not registered as a recognized cluster event type. This causes two downstream problems:\n\n1. **Missing GVK constant** (line 92-96): The following GVK constants are defined for DRA:\n   - `PodSchedulingContext`\n   - `ResourceClaim`\n   - `ResourceClass`\n   - `ResourceClaimParameters`\n   - `ResourceClassParameters`\n   - **But NOT `ResourceSlice`**\n\n2. **Missing in UnrollWildCardResource()** (line 187-191): The function that expands wildcard events includes ResourceClaim, ResourceClass, etc., but **NOT ResourceSlice**.\n\nThis cascades into two additional files where ResourceSlice events cannot be properly handled:\n\n**Secondary Issue**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go:395-543`\n- The `addAllEventHandlers()` function has a switch statement that handles GVK types\n- It has cases for ResourceClass, ResourceClaimParameters, ResourceClassParameters, etc.\n- **But no case for ResourceSlice** \u2014 so even if ResourceSlice was a valid GVK, no informer handler would be registered\n\n**Tertiary Issue**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go:381-413`\n- The `EventsToRegister()` method returns events that should trigger pod rescheduling\n- It includes: ResourceClaimParameters, ResourceClassParameters, ResourceClaim, PodSchedulingContext, Node, ResourceClass\n- **But NOT ResourceSlice** \u2014 so the plugin never signals the scheduler queue to retry pods when ResourceSlices are created/updated\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### Fix 1: Add ResourceSlice GVK constant\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n\n```diff\nconst (\n\tPod GVK = \"Pod\"\n\tNode                    GVK = \"Node\"\n\tPersistentVolume        GVK = \"PersistentVolume\"\n\tPersistentVolumeClaim   GVK = \"PersistentVolumeClaim\"\n\tCSINode                 GVK = \"storage.k8s.io/CSINode\"\n\tCSIDriver               GVK = \"storage.k8s.io/CSIDriver\"\n\tCSIStorageCapacity      GVK = \"storage.k8s.io/CSIStorageCapacity\"\n\tStorageClass            GVK = \"storage.k8s.io/StorageClass\"\n\tPodSchedulingContext    GVK = \"PodSchedulingContext\"\n\tResourceClaim           GVK = \"ResourceClaim\"\n\tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n\tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n\tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"\n\n\tWildCard GVK = \"*\"\n)\n```\n\n### Fix 2: Add ResourceSlice to UnrollWildCardResource()\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n\n```diff\nfunc UnrollWildCardResource() []ClusterEventWithHint {\n\treturn []ClusterEventWithHint{\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: Pod, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: Node, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PersistentVolume, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PersistentVolumeClaim, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSINode, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSIDriver, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSIStorageCapacity, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: StorageClass, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PodSchedulingContext, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClaim, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClass, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClassParameters, ActionType: All}},\n+\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceSlice, ActionType: All}},\n\t}\n}\n```\n\n### Fix 3: Add ResourceSlice event handler registration\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`\n\n```diff\n\tfor gvk, at := range gvkMap {\n\t\tswitch gvk {\n\t\tcase framework.Node, framework.Pod:\n\t\t\t// Do nothing.\n\t\tcase framework.CSINode:\n\t\t\t// ... handle CSINode ...\n\t\t// ... other cases ...\n\t\tcase framework.ResourceClassParameters:\n\t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n\t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClassParameters().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n\t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceClassParameters, \"ResourceClassParameters\"),\n\t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n\t\t\t}\n+\t\tcase framework.ResourceSlice:\n+\t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n+\t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n+\t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceSlice, \"ResourceSlice\"),\n+\t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n+\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n+\t\t\t\t}\n+\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n+\t\t\t}\n\t\tcase framework.StorageClass:\n\t\t\t// ... handle StorageClass ...\n```\n\n### Fix 4: Register ResourceSlice events in DRA plugin\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n\n```diff\nfunc (pl *dynamicResources) EventsToRegister() []framework.ClusterEventWithHint {\n\tif !pl.enabled {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\n\tevents := []framework.ClusterEventWithHint{\n\t\t// Changes for claim or class parameters creation may make pods\n\t\t// schedulable which depend on claims using those parameters.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimParametersChange},\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClassParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClassParametersChange},\n\n\t\t// Allocation is tracked in ResourceClaims, so any changes may make the pods schedulable.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaim, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimChange},\n\t\t// When a driver has provided additional information, a pod waiting for that information\n\t\t// may be schedulable.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.PodSchedulingContext, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterPodSchedulingContextChange},\n\t\t// A resource might depend on node labels for topology filtering.\n\t\t// A new or updated node may make pods schedulable.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.Node, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.UpdateNodeLabel | framework.UpdateNodeTaint}},\n\t\t// A pod might be waiting for a class to get created or modified.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClass, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n+\t\t// ResourceSlices published by drivers contain available resources.\n+\t\t// A new or updated ResourceSlice may make pods schedulable.\n+\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange},\n\t}\n\treturn events\n}\n```\n\n(Additionally, implement `pl.isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange()` method with similar logic to other change detection methods.)\n\n## Analysis\n\n### The Bug's Lifecycle\n\n1. **Pod Creation**: A pod requesting DRA resources is created before the DRA driver starts\n2. **Initial Scheduling Attempt** (line ~111 in schedule_one.go):\n   - The scheduler calls `schedulingCycle()`\n   - The DRA plugin's PreEnqueue/Filter phases check for available ResourceSlices\n   - No ResourceSlices exist yet \u2192 pod marked as Unschedulable\n3. **Pod Queuing**: The pod is added to the unschedulable queue with the reason \"cannot allocate all claims\"\n4. **Driver Starts**: The DRA driver boots up and creates ResourceSlice objects to advertise available resources\n5. **ResourceSlice Events (BUG HERE)**:\n   - The ResourceSlice informer detects Add/Update events\n   - But there is **NO event handler registered** for ResourceSlice (missing from eventhandlers.go)\n   - Even if a handler existed, the **DRA plugin doesn't register for ResourceSlice events** (missing from EventsToRegister())\n6. **Pod Stuck**: The scheduler never re-evaluates the pod because no one told the scheduler queue that something relevant changed\n7. **Result**: Pod remains permanently in Unschedulable state despite resources now being available\n\n### Why This Happens\n\nThe scheduler uses an event-driven architecture where cluster resources can trigger re-evaluation of unschedulable pods. The mechanism works like this:\n\n1. When a pod fails scheduling, it's added to the `unschedulablePods` pool\n2. When relevant cluster events occur (e.g., Node resource changes), the scheduler queue is notified\n3. The queue calls `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` to retry unschedulable pods\n4. For this to work, each plugin must register which events are relevant to it via `EventsToRegister()`\n5. The scheduler framework must have event handlers that listen to those events and signal the queue\n\nResourceSlice events are critical for DRA scheduling because:\n- ResourceSlices advertise node-local resources available to a driver\n- When a driver starts, it publishes ResourceSlices showing what resources it manages\n- Pods waiting for those resources need to be retried when the ResourceSlices appear\n- Without this wiring, pods become permanently stuck\n\nThe fix is to add ResourceSlice to all three layers of event handling in the scheduler.\n",
  "file_path": "/logs/agent/solution.md"

handle CSINode ...\n\t\t// ... other cases ...\n\t\tcase framework.ResourceClassParameters:\n\t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n\t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClassParameters().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n\t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceClassParameters, \"ResourceClassParameters\"),\n\t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n\t\t\t}\n+\t\tcase framework.ResourceSlice:\n+\t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n+\t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n+\t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceSlice, \"ResourceSlice\"),\n+\t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n+\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n+\t\t\t\t}\n+\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n+\t\t\t}\n\t\tcase framework.StorageClass:\n\t\t\t// ... handle StorageClass ...\n```\n\n### Fix 4: Register ResourceSlice events in DRA plugin\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n\n```diff\nfunc (pl *dynamicResources) EventsToRegister() []framework.ClusterEventWithHint {\n\tif !pl.enabled {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\n\tevents := []framework.ClusterEventWithHint{\n\t\t// Changes for claim or class parameters creation may make pods\n\t\t// schedulable which depend on claims using those parameters.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimParametersChange},\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClassParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClassParametersChange},\n\n\t\t// Allocation is tracked in ResourceClaims, so any changes may make the pods schedulable.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaim, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimChange},\n\t\t// When a driver has provided additional information, a pod waiting for that information\n\t\t// may be schedulable.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.PodSchedulingContext, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterPodSchedulingContextChange},\n\t\t// A resource might depend on node labels for topology filtering.\n\t\t// A new or updated node may make pods schedulable.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.Node, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.UpdateNodeLabel | framework.UpdateNodeTaint}},\n\t\t// A pod might be waiting for a class to get created or modified.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClass, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n+\t\t// ResourceSlices published by drivers contain available resources.\n+\t\t// A new or updated ResourceSlice may make pods schedulable.\n+\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange},\n\t}\n\treturn events\n}\n```\n\n(Additionally, implement `pl.isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange()` method with similar logic to other change detection methods.)\n\n## Analysis\n\n### The Bug's Lifecycle\n\n1. **Pod Creation**: A pod requesting DRA resources is created before the DRA driver starts\n2. **Initial Scheduling Attempt** (line ~111 in schedule_one.go):\n   - The scheduler calls `schedulingCycle()`\n   - The DRA plugin's PreEnqueue/Filter phases check for available ResourceSlices\n   - No ResourceSlices exist yet \u2192 pod marked as Unschedulable\n3. **Pod Queuing**: The pod is added to the unschedulable queue with the reason \"cannot allocate all claims\"\n4. **Driver Starts**: The DRA driver boots up and creates ResourceSlice objects to advertise available resources\n5. **ResourceSlice Events (BUG HERE)**:\n   - The ResourceSlice informer detects Add/Update events\n   - But there is **NO event handler registered** for ResourceSlice (missing from eventhandlers.go)\n   - Even if a handler existed, the **DRA plugin doesn't register for ResourceSlice events** (missing from EventsToRegister())\n6. **Pod Stuck**: The scheduler never re-evaluates the pod because no one told the scheduler queue that something relevant changed\n7. **Result**: Pod remains permanently in Unschedulable state despite resources now being available\n\n### Why This Happens\n\nThe scheduler uses an event-driven architecture where cluster resources can trigger re-evaluation of unschedulable pods. The mechanism works like this:\n\n1. When a pod fails scheduling, it's added to the `unschedulablePods` pool\n2. When relevant cluster events occur (e.g., Node resource changes), the scheduler queue is notified\n3. The queue calls `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` to retry unschedulable pods\n4. For this to work, each plugin must register which events are relevant to it via `EventsToRegister()`\n5. The scheduler framework must have event handlers that listen to those events and signal the queue\n\nResourceSlice events are critical for DRA scheduling because:\n- ResourceSlices advertise node-local resources available to a driver\n- When a driver starts, it publishes ResourceSlices showing what resources it manages\n- Pods waiting for those resources need to be retried when the ResourceSlices appear\n- Without this wiring, pods become permanently stuck\n\nThe fix is to add ResourceSlice to all three layers of event handling in the scheduler.\n",

## Files Examined

- `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` — Entry point for scheduling cycle; calls `ScheduleOne()` which invokes `schedulingCycle()` that calls `SchedulePod()`, which eventually checks resource allocation status
- `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` — Registers event handlers for cluster resources; examined the `addAllEventHandlers()` function that sets up handlers for various resource types including Dynamic Resource Allocation resources

- `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` — Scheduler initialization (referenced for context)
- `staging/src/k8s.io/api/resource/v1alpha2/types.go` — ResourceSlice API type definition (confirmed it exists)
